If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n//    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n//    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n// 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n//    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n// 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n//    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n// 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n//    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n// 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n//    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n//    was configured to ignore errors.\n//\n// In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n// using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n// maintain state.\n\nservice ExternalProcessor {\n  // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n  // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\n  // protocol is described by the ProcessingRequest and ProcessingResponse\n  // messages below.\n  rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n  }\n}\n\n// This represents the different types of messages that Envoy can send\n// to an external processing server.\n// [#next-free-field: 11]\nmessage ProcessingRequest {\n  reserved 1;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Which\n  // ones are set for a particular HTTP request/response depend on the\n  // processing mode.\n  oneof request {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Information about the HTTP request headers, as well as peer info and additional\n    // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n    // HeaderResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\n\n    // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\n    // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\n    // HeaderResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP request body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is true, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\n    HttpBody request_body = 4;\n\n    // A chunk of the HTTP response body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back\n    // a BodyResponse message or close the stream.\n    HttpBody response_body = 5;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the request path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\n    // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\n    //\n    // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\n    // the original downstream request has trailers.\n    HttpTrailers request_trailers = 6;\n\n    // The HTTP trailers for the response path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\n    // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\n    //\n    // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":389}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01ARQ2nY4UQbnXvMtzNKRbfA","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01PVsHmnbmhLbwgqUfHABHfM","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Migration Guide: Envoy ext_proc HTTP Filter — v1.30.0 to v1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis guide covers the changes to the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** between Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024) and v1.31.0 (July 2024). The migration involves one breaking behavioral change, one deprecation requiring action, several new configuration fields, and significant improvements to observability mode.\n\n**Summary of major changes:**\n\n| Category | Change |\n|---|---|\n| Breaking (behavioral) | Message timeout now returns HTTP 504 instead of HTTP 500 |\n| Breaking (proto type) | `ImmediateResponse.body` field type changed from `string` to `bytes` |\n| Deprecated | `disable_clear_route_cache` superseded by `route_cache_action` |\n| New field | `route_cache_action` — fine-grained route cache control |\n| New field | `deferred_close_timeout` — observability mode stream lifecycle |\n| New feature | Observability mode fully implemented (deferred stream close, flow control) |\n| New runtime flag | `envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control` |\n| Internal change | gRPC stream lifecycle managed via thread-local `ThreadLocalStreamManager` |\n\n**Relevant source paths compared:**\n\n- Proto API: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- Service API: `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Message Timeout Error Response Changed from HTTP 500 to HTTP 504\n\n**Affected component:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` — `Filter::onMessageTimeout()`\n\n**What changed:**\n\nWhen the per-message timeout expires (i.e., the external processor does not respond within the `message_timeout` window) and `failure_mode_allow` is `false`, Envoy previously returned an HTTP **500 Internal Server Error** to the downstream client. In v1.31.0, this was corrected to return HTTP **504 Gateway Timeout**, which more accurately represents a timeout waiting for an upstream service.\n\n**v1.30.0 behavior:**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 behavior:**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 504 Gateway Timeout\n```\n\n**Impact:** Any downstream clients, monitoring systems, or alerting rules that differentiate between 500 and 504 responses will observe a change. If your SLOs or dashboards track 5xx breakdown by status code, update them to expect 504 for ext_proc timeout events.\n\n**Action required:**\n\n- Update any client-side error handling or retry policies that specifically match HTTP 500 for ext_proc timeout scenarios.\n- Update monitoring dashboards and alerts that filter on `response_code == 500` for ext_proc timeout attribution.\n- The `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` access log field will still contain `ext_proc_error_per-message_timeout_exceeded` to identify the source regardless of status code.\n\n**No configuration change is required** — this is purely a behavioral correction.\n\n---\n\n### 2. `ImmediateResponse.body` Field Type Changed from `string` to `bytes`\n\n**Affected component:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto` — `ImmediateResponse` message, field 3\n\n**What changed:**\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;   // <-- was string\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n\n// v1.31.0\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;    // <-- now bytes\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** In most protobuf language bindings (Go, Java, Python, C++), `string` and `bytes` are wire-compatible (both use wire type 2/length-delimited). However, the generated accessor types differ:\n\n- **Go:** `string` → `[]byte`\n- **Java:** `String` → `ByteString`\n- **Python:** `str` (unicode) → `bytes`\n- **C++:** `std::string` → `std::string` (unchanged at wire level, but semantic difference)\n\n**Action required:**\n\n- Audit external processor implementations that set `ImmediateResponse.body`.\n- Update code that assigns a string literal to this field to explicitly encode it as bytes (e.g., `[]byte(\"error message\")` in Go, `ByteString.copyFromUtf8(\"error message\")` in Java).\n- Regenerate protobuf bindings from the v1.31 proto definitions before rebuilding your external processor.\n\n**Before (Go example):**\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &envoy_type.HttpStatus{Code: envoy_type.StatusCode_BadRequest},\n    Body:   \"Invalid request\",  // string\n}\n```\n\n**After (Go example):**\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &envoy_type.HttpStatus{Code: envoy_type.StatusCode_BadRequest},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Invalid request\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### `disable_clear_route_cache` — Use `route_cache_action` Instead\n\n**Affected component:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto` — `ExternalProcessor` message, field 11\n\n**What changed:**\n\nThe boolean field `disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11) is now marked with a `udpa.annotations.field_migrate` annotation indicating it is being promoted into a `oneof` called `clear_route_cache_type`. A new enum field `route_cache_action` (field 18) has been added that supersedes it with more explicit, multi-value semantics.\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n// v1.31.0 — still present but deprecated in favor of route_cache_action\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n```\n\nThe new `RouteCacheAction` enum (defined inside `ExternalProcessor`) provides three explicit values:\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default: clear the route cache only when the clear_route_cache bit\n  // is set in the external processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache, regardless of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache, regardless of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response. Equivalent to\n  // disable_clear_route_cache = true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n**Validation behavior:** If both `disable_clear_route_cache = true` and `route_cache_action` is set to a non-`DEFAULT` value simultaneously, Envoy will throw a configuration error at startup:\n\n```\ndisable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\n```\n\nInternally, if only `disable_clear_route_cache = true` is set, the implementation converts it to `route_cache_action = RETAIN` at filter construction time.\n\n**Migration advice:**\n\nReplace `disable_clear_route_cache` with `route_cache_action`:\n\n**Before (v1.30.0):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0 — recommended):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\nIf you previously relied on the default behavior (allowing `clear_route_cache` from the processor to take effect), no action is needed — `DEFAULT` is the zero value and does not need to be set explicitly.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. `route_cache_action` — Fine-Grained Route Cache Control\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action` (field 18, type `RouteCacheAction` enum)\n\n**Source:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nThis new field gives operators explicit control over how the route cache interacts with ext_proc responses. The three modes are:\n\n| Value | Behavior |\n|---|---|\n| `DEFAULT` (0) | Route cache cleared only when `clear_route_cache = true` in the processor response |\n| `CLEAR` (1) | Route cache always cleared when processing request headers, unconditionally |\n| `RETAIN` (2) | Route cache never cleared, even if the processor sets `clear_route_cache = true` |\n\n**When to use `CLEAR`:** Use when your external processor always modifies routing-relevant headers (e.g., `:authority`, `host`) and you want to guarantee routing is re-evaluated without requiring the processor to set the `clear_route_cache` bit on every response.\n\n**When to use `RETAIN`:** Use when your processing is read-only or the processor should never be able to affect routing decisions, providing a security boundary.\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR   # Always re-evaluate routing after ext_proc response\n```\n\n---\n\n### 2. `deferred_close_timeout` — Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle Control\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.deferred_close_timeout` (field 19, type `google.protobuf.Duration`)\n\n**Source:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Default value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n\nThis field controls how long Envoy holds open a gRPC stream to the external processor after the associated HTTP stream has ended, when operating in `observability_mode = true`. In observability mode, the side-channel gRPC stream to the processor may outlive the client-to-backend HTTP stream. Without a timeout, these orphaned streams could accumulate and exhaust resources.\n\nWhen `observability_mode` is enabled:\n\n1. On filter destruction, instead of immediately closing the gRPC stream, Envoy defers the closure using a timer.\n2. The timer fires after `deferred_close_timeout`, at which point the stream is closed and removed from the `ThreadLocalStreamManager`.\n3. If the external processor closes the stream first, the timer is cancelled.\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s   # Hold stream open up to 10s after HTTP stream ends\n```\n\n**Tuning guidance:**\n- Set this higher if your external processor needs more time to complete in-flight async work after the HTTP stream closes.\n- Set this lower in high-traffic environments to bound resource consumption from deferred streams.\n- A value of `0s` is not recommended as it would immediately close the stream, defeating the purpose of deferred closure.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Observability Mode — Full Implementation\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.observability_mode` (field 17, type `bool`) — existed in v1.30 but partially implemented\n\n**Source:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n\nIn v1.30.0, `observability_mode` was introduced but carried a warning that flow control was not yet implemented. In v1.31.0, observability mode receives a complete implementation overhaul:\n\n**What is observability mode?**\n\nWhen `observability_mode = true`, ext_proc operates in \"fire and forget\" mode:\n\n- Envoy sends HTTP data (headers, body chunks, trailers) to the external processor without pausing the filter chain.\n- The external processor **must not** send responses back — any responses received are silently ignored.\n- The `message_timeout` restriction does not apply.\n- The processor can close the stream to signal no more data is needed.\n\n**v1.31.0 improvements:**\n\n1. **Full header/body/trailer support in observability mode:** In v1.31, all three message types are sent with `observability_mode = true` set in `ProcessingRequest`, so the processor can identify fire-and-forget messages.\n\n2. **Deferred stream closure** (via `ThreadLocalStreamManager`): Streams are no longer immediately closed on filter destruction; they are handed off to a thread-local manager and closed after `deferred_close_timeout`.\n\n3. **`notifyFilterDestroy()` callback:** When the filter is destroyed, the gRPC stream's `callbacks_` reference (back to the filter) is reset to an `OptRef` null to prevent dangling references after deferred closure.\n\n4. **`grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag** (see New Runtime Flags below).\n\n5. **`encodeComplete()` hook:** The filter now logs gRPC stream info when encoding completes in observability mode.\n\n**Body processing restriction:** In observability mode, only `STREAMED` body processing mode is supported. If `BUFFERED` or `BUFFERED_PARTIAL` is configured, it is silently ignored. `NONE` (skip body) continues to work normally.\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: my_traffic_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n    request_trailer_mode: SEND\n    response_trailer_mode: SEND\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. `observability_mode` Field in `ProcessingRequest`\n\n**Proto field:** `ProcessingRequest.observability_mode` (field 10, type `bool`)\n\n**Source:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n\nThis field was already present in v1.30 but is now actively set by the filter when operating in observability mode. External processors should check this flag to determine whether they are expected to send a response.\n\n```protobuf\n// In ProcessingRequest (service proto)\nbool observability_mode = 10;\n```\n\nWhen this field is `true` in a `ProcessingRequest`:\n- The processor **must not** send a `ProcessingResponse` — any response will be discarded.\n- The processor may still close the gRPC stream.\n\n**External processor update:** Servers should handle this flag gracefully:\n\n```go\n// Example external processor server logic\nfunc (s *server) Process(stream ext_proc.ExternalProcessor_ProcessServer) error {\n    for {\n        req, err := stream.Recv()\n        if err == io.EOF {\n            return nil\n        }\n        if err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n\n        // In observability mode, do not send a response\n        if req.ObservabilityMode {\n            // Just observe/log/record metrics — do not call stream.Send()\n            s.recordMetrics(req)\n            continue\n        }\n\n        // Normal processing path\n        resp := s.processRequest(req)\n        if err := stream.Send(resp); err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. New Runtime Feature Flag: `grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n\n**Flag name:** `envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n\n**Source:** `source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.h`\n\nThis new reloadable feature flag (enabled by default) activates gRPC watermark-based flow control for ext_proc side streams. When enabled:\n\n- The gRPC stream is configured with watermark callbacks tied to the decoder filter's watermark callbacks.\n- This prevents a fast HTTP sender (downstream client or upstream server) from overwhelming a slower external processor.\n- When the stream is closed, watermark callbacks are removed cleanly.\n\nThis addresses the flow control gap that was called out as a warning in v1.30's `observability_mode` documentation (`https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319`).\n\n**To disable (if experiencing issues):**\n```yaml\n# In Envoy's layered runtime configuration\nlayered_runtime:\n  layers:\n    - name: static_layer\n      static_layer:\n        envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control: false\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. gRPC Stream Client API Enhancements\n\n**Source:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client.h`, `client_impl.h`, `client_impl.cc`\n\nThe internal gRPC client interface was updated to support richer stream creation options and safer lifecycle management.\n\n**`ExternalProcessorStream::notifyFilterDestroy()`** — New virtual method:\n\nThe `ExternalProcessorStream` interface gained a `notifyFilterDestroy()` method. When the filter is destroyed, it calls this method on the stream, which resets the `OptRef<ExternalProcessorCallbacks>` to prevent use-after-free when deferred stream callbacks arrive after filter destruction.\n\n**`ExternalProcessorClient::start()` signature change:**\n\n```cpp\n// v1.30.0\nExternalProcessorStreamPtr start(\n    ExternalProcessorCallbacks& callbacks,\n    const Grpc::GrpcServiceConfigWithHashKey& config_with_hash_key,\n    const StreamInfo::StreamInfo& stream_info);\n\n// v1.31.0\nExternalProcessorStreamPtr start(\n    ExternalProcessorCallbacks& callbacks,\n    const Grpc::GrpcServiceConfigWithHashKey& config_with_hash_key,\n    const Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions& options,\n    Http::DecoderFilterWatermarkCallbacks* decoder_watermark_callbacks);\n```\n\nThis is an internal API change. It affects anyone who has written a custom `ExternalProcessorClient` implementation (e.g., for testing). The `StreamOptions` now carries parent span, parent context, and buffer-for-retry settings that were previously assembled inside `startStream()`. The `decoder_watermark_callbacks` parameter supports the new flow control feature.\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Summary of Proto Field Changes in `ExternalProcessor`\n\n| Field | Number | v1.30 | v1.31 | Action |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| `grpc_service` | 1 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `failure_mode_allow` | 2 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `processing_mode` | 3 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `request_attributes` | 5 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `response_attributes` | 6 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `message_timeout` | 7 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `stat_prefix` | 8 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `mutation_rules` | 9 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `max_message_timeout` | 10 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | 11 | Present | **Deprecated** | Migrate to `route_cache_action` |\n| `forward_rules` | 12 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `filter_metadata` | 13 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `allow_mode_override` | 14 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `disable_immediate_response` | 15 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `metadata_options` | 16 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `observability_mode` | 17 | Present (partial) | Present (full) | Review if using |\n| `route_cache_action` | 18 | **Absent** | **New** | Use instead of `disable_clear_route_cache` |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | 19 | **Absent** | **New** | Configure if using observability mode |\n\n### Minimal v1.30 → v1.31 Configuration Diff\n\nFor a configuration that previously used `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n```yaml\n# Before (v1.30.0)\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      message_timeout: 0.2s\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true    # <-- to migrate\n\n# After (v1.31.0)\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      message_timeout: 0.2s\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN         # <-- replaces disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nFor a configuration using `observability_mode`, add `deferred_close_timeout`:\n\n```yaml\n# Before (v1.30.0)\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n\n# After (v1.31.0) — add deferred_close_timeout\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s   # <-- new; 5s is the default if omitted\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle\n\nIn v1.30, the gRPC stream opened in `observability_mode` was closed synchronously when the HTTP filter was destroyed (`onDestroy()`). In v1.31, destruction calls `deferredCloseStream()` instead, which hands the stream to `ThreadLocalStreamManager`. The manager starts a timer and closes the stream after `deferred_close_timeout` elapses. This means:\n\n- External processors in observability mode will continue to receive in-flight data for up to `deferred_close_timeout` after the HTTP request completes.\n- Prometheus/stats: `streams_closed` counter is now incremented by the deferred timer callback, not at filter destruction time.\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Responses Are Silently Discarded\n\nIn v1.31, if an external processor sends a `ProcessingResponse` when `observability_mode = true` was set in the corresponding `ProcessingRequest`, the response is logged and discarded:\n\n```\n// From ext_proc.cc in v1.31:\nif (config_->observabilityMode()) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Ignoring received message when observability mode is enabled\");\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nIn v1.30, response handling logic in observability mode was less clearly defined and could lead to unexpected state transitions.\n\n### 3. `openStream()` Now Passes Parent Span and Context\n\nThe `openStream()` call now creates `Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions` with the active span and stream info from the decoder callbacks, enabling proper distributed tracing propagation through the ext_proc gRPC call. In v1.30, only stream info was passed; the parent span was not threaded through.\n\n### 4. Deferred Stream Callback Safety\n\nIn v1.30, if the ext_proc gRPC stream received a message (e.g., `onReceiveMessage`) after the parent filter was destroyed, this could access a dangling reference. In v1.31, `ExternalProcessorStreamImpl::callbacks_` is changed from `ExternalProcessorCallbacks&` (reference) to `OptRef<ExternalProcessorCallbacks>` (optional reference). When `notifyFilterDestroy()` is called, the optional is cleared, and all subsequent callbacks check `callbacks_.has_value()` before dispatching.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Update Proto Definitions and Regenerate Bindings\n\nIf you maintain a custom external processor server or use go-control-plane / Java control plane:\n\n1. Update your dependency on `envoy/api` or `go-control-plane` to a version built from Envoy v1.31 protos.\n2. Regenerate protobuf language bindings.\n3. Fix any compile errors related to `ImmediateResponse.body` type change (`string` → `bytes`).\n\n### Step 2: Update `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`\n\nSearch your Envoy configurations for `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n```bash\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/envoy/configs/\n```\n\nFor each occurrence:\n- Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: true` with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- Remove `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (this is equivalent to the default `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`)\n\n**Validation:** Setting both fields simultaneously (e.g., `disable_clear_route_cache: true` and `route_cache_action: CLEAR`) will cause a startup error. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` entirely when using `route_cache_action`.\n\n### Step 3: Update Monitoring for Timeout Errors\n\nUpdate any alerting rules or dashboards that identify ext_proc timeout events by HTTP 500 status code:\n\n1. Change the filter from `response_code == 500` to `response_code == 504` for timeout attribution.\n2. Alternatively, use the `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` access log field matching `ext_proc_error_per-message_timeout_exceeded` — this is stable across the version change.\n\n### Step 4: Configure `deferred_close_timeout` for Observability Mode\n\nIf using `observability_mode: true`, explicitly set `deferred_close_timeout` to match your processor's expected processing latency:\n\n```yaml\n# If your processor needs up to 3 seconds to finalize after stream end:\ndeferred_close_timeout: 3s\n```\n\nIf omitted, the default of 5 seconds applies. In high-traffic environments, tune this value down to limit resource usage from deferred streams.\n\n### Step 5: Update External Processor Servers for Observability Mode\n\nIf your external processor server is used in observability mode, update it to:\n\n1. Check `ProcessingRequest.observability_mode` before sending a `ProcessingResponse`.\n2. Skip sending a response when `observability_mode == true`.\n3. Continue reading from the stream (the stream may stay open longer than the HTTP request lifetime).\n\n### Step 6: Evaluate `grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n\nThe new `grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag is enabled by default. Monitor your ext_proc gRPC stream metrics after upgrading. If you observe unexpected stream pausing or throughput reduction:\n\n1. Check if your external processor is slow to consume data (this is what flow control is protecting against).\n2. If the flag causes issues in your environment, disable it via runtime override while investigating.\n\n### Step 7: Regenerate and Validate Configurations\n\nRun Envoy's configuration validation mode after applying changes:\n\n```bash\nenvoy --mode validate -c /path/to/envoy.yaml\n```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Verify Timeout Error Code\n\nWrite an integration test that:\n1. Configures ext_proc with a very short `message_timeout` (e.g., `1ms`) and `failure_mode_allow: false`.\n2. Points at a mock processor that never responds.\n3. Sends an HTTP request through Envoy.\n4. Asserts the response is **HTTP 504** (not 500).\n\n### 2. Verify `ImmediateResponse.body` Encoding\n\nIf your processor sends `ImmediateResponse` with a body:\n1. Send a request that triggers an immediate response from the processor.\n2. Verify the response body is correctly decoded by the downstream client.\n3. Test with non-ASCII content to confirm binary-safe handling.\n\n### 3. Verify `route_cache_action` Behavior\n\nFor each `route_cache_action` value:\n- **`DEFAULT`:** Verify routing changes only when processor sets `clear_route_cache = true`.\n- **`CLEAR`:** Verify routing is re-evaluated on every ext_proc request header response.\n- **`RETAIN`:** Verify routing is never changed regardless of `clear_route_cache` in processor response.\n\n### 4. Verify Observability Mode Deferred Close\n\nIf using observability mode:\n1. Send a request through Envoy with a processor that logs stream lifecycle events.\n2. Verify the processor continues to receive data after the HTTP stream completes.\n3. Verify the gRPC stream closes within `deferred_close_timeout` after the HTTP stream ends.\n4. Monitor the `streams_closed` stat counter — it should increment after the deferred timeout, not immediately on request completion.\n\n### 5. Verify `disable_clear_route_cache` Backward Compatibility\n\nIf you left `disable_clear_route_cache: true` in your config (without removing it), verify:\n1. Envoy starts without error (it converts it to `RETAIN` internally).\n2. The behavior is equivalent to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\n**Warning:** Do not set both `disable_clear_route_cache: true` and `route_cache_action: CLEAR/RETAIN` simultaneously — this will cause a startup panic.\n\n### 6. Test with Updated go-control-plane / Java Bindings\n\nIf using a control plane:\n1. Build your control plane against the v1.31 proto bindings.\n2. Push an ext_proc configuration and verify Envoy applies it without xDS rejection.\n3. Check xDS logs for any unknown field warnings.\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Rolling Back to v1.30.0\n\nIf you need to revert from v1.31.0 to v1.30.0 after an upgrade:\n\n**1. Configuration rollback:**\n\n| v1.31 Field | v1.30 Equivalent |\n|---|---|\n| `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | `disable_clear_route_cache: true` |\n| `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | *(omit `disable_clear_route_cache`)* |\n| `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | *(no equivalent — remove and accept DEFAULT behavior)* |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | *(remove field — not recognized by v1.30)* |\n\nRemove `route_cache_action` and `deferred_close_timeout` before deploying v1.30.0. Envoy v1.30 will reject configurations containing unknown fields if strict validation is enabled.\n\n**2. Proto binding rollback:**\n\nRevert `ImmediateResponse.body` back to `string` type in your processor's generated code. Roll back to v1.30 protobuf definitions.\n\n**3. Monitoring rollback:**\n\nRestore any dashboards or alerts that were updated to expect HTTP 504 for ext_proc timeouts back to HTTP 500.\n\n**4. Feature flag rollback:**\n\nThe `grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag does not exist in v1.30 — remove any runtime override that references it.\n\n### Risk Assessment\n\n| Change | Rollback Risk | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| `route_cache_action` field | Low | Simply remove from config before rolling back |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` field | Low | Remove from config; no behavioral change until observability_mode is also used |\n| `ImmediateResponse.body` type | Medium | Requires proto binding rollback and code recompilation |\n| HTTP 504 timeout response | Low | Purely behavioral; update monitoring before rollback |\n| `grpc_side_stream_flow_control` | Low | Remove runtime override |\n\n---\n\n## Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n1. **Setting both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`:** This causes a runtime `EnvoyException` at filter construction. Always remove `disable_clear_route_cache` when using `route_cache_action`.\n\n2. **External processor responding in observability mode:** Processors that send `ProcessingResponse` messages when `ProcessingRequest.observability_mode == true` will have their responses silently dropped. This is a behavior change from v1.30 where the response handling was undefined — if your processor relied on sending responses in observability mode, it must be updated.\n\n3. **Assuming `BUFFERED` body mode works in observability mode:** Only `STREAMED` is supported for body processing in observability mode. `BUFFERED` and `BUFFERED_PARTIAL` are silently ignored when `observability_mode = true`. Verify your `processing_mode` configuration.\n\n4. **`deferred_close_timeout` too short for slow processors:** If `deferred_close_timeout` is set lower than the time your processor needs to process the last messages, data may be lost. Monitor `streams_closed` counter timing in relation to request completion to tune this value.\n\n5. **Ignoring the `ImmediateResponse.body` type change in statically-typed languages:** Go and Java will produce compile errors immediately, but dynamically-typed language bindings (e.g., Python with proto3) may silently encode incorrectly. Always regenerate and test bindings explicitly.\n\n6. **Not updating access log parsing for timeout details:** The `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` string `ext_proc_error_per-message_timeout_exceeded` is unchanged, but the HTTP status code changed from 500 to 504. Any log parsing that uses both fields together for ext_proc timeout detection needs to be updated.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":498,"cache_read_input_tokens":69625,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":498,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5ca8c2a9-154c-41e1-9798-70ee29acd74e","uuid":"763d74ca-3138-4469-bf52-d33d2b0db857"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01PVsHmnbmhLbwgqUfHABHfM","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/documentation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5ca8c2a9-154c-41e1-9798-70ee29acd74e","uuid":"a2131cfa-12c8-4f1d-9820-4f867f211b31","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Migration Guide: Envoy ext_proc HTTP Filter — v1.30.0 to v1.31.0\n\n## Overview\n\nThis guide covers the changes to the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** between Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024) and v1.31.0 (July 2024). The migration involves one breaking behavioral change, one deprecation requiring action, several new configuration fields, and significant improvements to observability mode.\n\n**Summary of major changes:**\n\n| Category | Change |\n|---|---|\n| Breaking (behavioral) | Message timeout now returns HTTP 504 instead of HTTP 500 |\n| Breaking (proto type) | `ImmediateResponse.body` field type changed from `string` to `bytes` |\n| Deprecated | `disable_clear_route_cache` superseded by `route_cache_action` |\n| New field | `route_cache_action` — fine-grained route cache control |\n| New field | `deferred_close_timeout` — observability mode stream lifecycle |\n| New feature | Observability mode fully implemented (deferred stream close, flow control) |\n| New runtime flag | `envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control` |\n| Internal change | gRPC stream lifecycle managed via thread-local `ThreadLocalStreamManager` |\n\n**Relevant source paths compared:**\n\n- Proto API: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- Service API: `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Message Timeout Error Response Changed from HTTP 500 to HTTP 504\n\n**Affected component:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` — `Filter::onMessageTimeout()`\n\n**What changed:**\n\nWhen the per-message timeout expires (i.e., the external processor does not respond within the `message_timeout` window) and `failure_mode_allow` is `false`, Envoy previously returned an HTTP **500 Internal Server Error** to the downstream client. In v1.31.0, this was corrected to return HTTP **504 Gateway Timeout**, which more accurately represents a timeout waiting for an upstream service.\n\n**v1.30.0 behavior:**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 500 Internal Server Error\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 behavior:**\n```\nHTTP/1.1 504 Gateway Timeout\n```\n\n**Impact:** Any downstream clients, monitoring systems, or alerting rules that differentiate between 500 and 504 responses will observe a change. If your SLOs or dashboards track 5xx breakdown by status code, update them to expect 504 for ext_proc timeout events.\n\n**Action required:**\n\n- Update any client-side error handling or retry policies that specifically match HTTP 500 for ext_proc timeout scenarios.\n- Update monitoring dashboards and alerts that filter on `response_code == 500` for ext_proc timeout attribution.\n- The `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` access log field will still contain `ext_proc_error_per-message_timeout_exceeded` to identify the source regardless of status code.\n\n**No configuration change is required** — this is purely a behavioral correction.\n\n---\n\n### 2. `ImmediateResponse.body` Field Type Changed from `string` to `bytes`\n\n**Affected component:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto` — `ImmediateResponse` message, field 3\n\n**What changed:**\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;   // <-- was string\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n\n// v1.31.0\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;    // <-- now bytes\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** In most protobuf language bindings (Go, Java, Python, C++), `string` and `bytes` are wire-compatible (both use wire type 2/length-delimited). However, the generated accessor types differ:\n\n- **Go:** `string` → `[]byte`\n- **Java:** `String` → `ByteString`\n- **Python:** `str` (unicode) → `bytes`\n- **C++:** `std::string` → `std::string` (unchanged at wire level, but semantic difference)\n\n**Action required:**\n\n- Audit external processor implementations that set `ImmediateResponse.body`.\n- Update code that assigns a string literal to this field to explicitly encode it as bytes (e.g., `[]byte(\"error message\")` in Go, `ByteString.copyFromUtf8(\"error message\")` in Java).\n- Regenerate protobuf bindings from the v1.31 proto definitions before rebuilding your external processor.\n\n**Before (Go example):**\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &envoy_type.HttpStatus{Code: envoy_type.StatusCode_BadRequest},\n    Body:   \"Invalid request\",  // string\n}\n```\n\n**After (Go example):**\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &envoy_type.HttpStatus{Code: envoy_type.StatusCode_BadRequest},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Invalid request\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### `disable_clear_route_cache` — Use `route_cache_action` Instead\n\n**Affected component:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto` — `ExternalProcessor` message, field 11\n\n**What changed:**\n\nThe boolean field `disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11) is now marked with a `udpa.annotations.field_migrate` annotation indicating it is being promoted into a `oneof` called `clear_route_cache_type`. A new enum field `route_cache_action` (field 18) has been added that supersedes it with more explicit, multi-value semantics.\n\n```protobuf\n// v1.30.0\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n// v1.31.0 — still present but deprecated in favor of route_cache_action\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n```\n\nThe new `RouteCacheAction` enum (defined inside `ExternalProcessor`) provides three explicit values:\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default: clear the route cache only when the clear_route_cache bit\n  // is set in the external processor response.\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache, regardless of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache, regardless of the clear_route_cache\n  // bit in the external processor response. Equivalent to\n  // disable_clear_route_cache = true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n**Validation behavior:** If both `disable_clear_route_cache = true` and `route_cache_action` is set to a non-`DEFAULT` value simultaneously, Envoy will throw a configuration error at startup:\n\n```\ndisable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\n```\n\nInternally, if only `disable_clear_route_cache = true` is set, the implementation converts it to `route_cache_action = RETAIN` at filter construction time.\n\n**Migration advice:**\n\nReplace `disable_clear_route_cache` with `route_cache_action`:\n\n**Before (v1.30.0):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31.0 — recommended):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\nIf you previously relied on the default behavior (allowing `clear_route_cache` from the processor to take effect), no action is needed — `DEFAULT` is the zero value and does not need to be set explicitly.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. `route_cache_action` — Fine-Grained Route Cache Control\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action` (field 18, type `RouteCacheAction` enum)\n\n**Source:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nThis new field gives operators explicit control over how the route cache interacts with ext_proc responses. The three modes are:\n\n| Value | Behavior |\n|---|---|\n| `DEFAULT` (0) | Route cache cleared only when `clear_route_cache = true` in the processor response |\n| `CLEAR` (1) | Route cache always cleared when processing request headers, unconditionally |\n| `RETAIN` (2) | Route cache never cleared, even if the processor sets `clear_route_cache = true` |\n\n**When to use `CLEAR`:** Use when your external processor always modifies routing-relevant headers (e.g., `:authority`, `host`) and you want to guarantee routing is re-evaluated without requiring the processor to set the `clear_route_cache` bit on every response.\n\n**When to use `RETAIN`:** Use when your processing is read-only or the processor should never be able to affect routing decisions, providing a security boundary.\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR   # Always re-evaluate routing after ext_proc response\n```\n\n---\n\n### 2. `deferred_close_timeout` — Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle Control\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.deferred_close_timeout` (field 19, type `google.protobuf.Duration`)\n\n**Source:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Default value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n\nThis field controls how long Envoy holds open a gRPC stream to the external processor after the associated HTTP stream has ended, when operating in `observability_mode = true`. In observability mode, the side-channel gRPC stream to the processor may outlive the client-to-backend HTTP stream. Without a timeout, these orphaned streams could accumulate and exhaust resources.\n\nWhen `observability_mode` is enabled:\n\n1. On filter destruction, instead of immediately closing the gRPC stream, Envoy defers the closure using a timer.\n2. The timer fires after `deferred_close_timeout`, at which point the stream is closed and removed from the `ThreadLocalStreamManager`.\n3. If the external processor closes the stream first, the timer is cancelled.\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s   # Hold stream open up to 10s after HTTP stream ends\n```\n\n**Tuning guidance:**\n- Set this higher if your external processor needs more time to complete in-flight async work after the HTTP stream closes.\n- Set this lower in high-traffic environments to bound resource consumption from deferred streams.\n- A value of `0s` is not recommended as it would immediately close the stream, defeating the purpose of deferred closure.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Observability Mode — Full Implementation\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.observability_mode` (field 17, type `bool`) — existed in v1.30 but partially implemented\n\n**Source:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n\nIn v1.30.0, `observability_mode` was introduced but carried a warning that flow control was not yet implemented. In v1.31.0, observability mode receives a complete implementation overhaul:\n\n**What is observability mode?**\n\nWhen `observability_mode = true`, ext_proc operates in \"fire and forget\" mode:\n\n- Envoy sends HTTP data (headers, body chunks, trailers) to the external processor without pausing the filter chain.\n- The external processor **must not** send responses back — any responses received are silently ignored.\n- The `message_timeout` restriction does not apply.\n- The processor can close the stream to signal no more data is needed.\n\n**v1.31.0 improvements:**\n\n1. **Full header/body/trailer support in observability mode:** In v1.31, all three message types are sent with `observability_mode = true` set in `ProcessingRequest`, so the processor can identify fire-and-forget messages.\n\n2. **Deferred stream closure** (via `ThreadLocalStreamManager`): Streams are no longer immediately closed on filter destruction; they are handed off to a thread-local manager and closed after `deferred_close_timeout`.\n\n3. **`notifyFilterDestroy()` callback:** When the filter is destroyed, the gRPC stream's `callbacks_` reference (back to the filter) is reset to an `OptRef` null to prevent dangling references after deferred closure.\n\n4. **`grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag** (see New Runtime Flags below).\n\n5. **`encodeComplete()` hook:** The filter now logs gRPC stream info when encoding completes in observability mode.\n\n**Body processing restriction:** In observability mode, only `STREAMED` body processing mode is supported. If `BUFFERED` or `BUFFERED_PARTIAL` is configured, it is silently ignored. `NONE` (skip body) continues to work normally.\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: my_traffic_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n    request_trailer_mode: SEND\n    response_trailer_mode: SEND\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. `observability_mode` Field in `ProcessingRequest`\n\n**Proto field:** `ProcessingRequest.observability_mode` (field 10, type `bool`)\n\n**Source:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n\nThis field was already present in v1.30 but is now actively set by the filter when operating in observability mode. External processors should check this flag to determine whether they are expected to send a response.\n\n```protobuf\n// In ProcessingRequest (service proto)\nbool observability_mode = 10;\n```\n\nWhen this field is `true` in a `ProcessingRequest`:\n- The processor **must not** send a `ProcessingResponse` — any response will be discarded.\n- The processor may still close the gRPC stream.\n\n**External processor update:** Servers should handle this flag gracefully:\n\n```go\n// Example external processor server logic\nfunc (s *server) Process(stream ext_proc.ExternalProcessor_ProcessServer) error {\n    for {\n        req, err := stream.Recv()\n        if err == io.EOF {\n            return nil\n        }\n        if err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n\n        // In observability mode, do not send a response\n        if req.ObservabilityMode {\n            // Just observe/log/record metrics — do not call stream.Send()\n            s.recordMetrics(req)\n            continue\n        }\n\n        // Normal processing path\n        resp := s.processRequest(req)\n        if err := stream.Send(resp); err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. New Runtime Feature Flag: `grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n\n**Flag name:** `envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n\n**Source:** `source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.h`\n\nThis new reloadable feature flag (enabled by default) activates gRPC watermark-based flow control for ext_proc side streams. When enabled:\n\n- The gRPC stream is configured with watermark callbacks tied to the decoder filter's watermark callbacks.\n- This prevents a fast HTTP sender (downstream client or upstream server) from overwhelming a slower external processor.\n- When the stream is closed, watermark callbacks are removed cleanly.\n\nThis addresses the flow control gap that was called out as a warning in v1.30's `observability_mode` documentation (`https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319`).\n\n**To disable (if experiencing issues):**\n```yaml\n# In Envoy's layered runtime configuration\nlayered_runtime:\n  layers:\n    - name: static_layer\n      static_layer:\n        envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control: false\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. gRPC Stream Client API Enhancements\n\n**Source:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client.h`, `client_impl.h`, `client_impl.cc`\n\nThe internal gRPC client interface was updated to support richer stream creation options and safer lifecycle management.\n\n**`ExternalProcessorStream::notifyFilterDestroy()`** — New virtual method:\n\nThe `ExternalProcessorStream` interface gained a `notifyFilterDestroy()` method. When the filter is destroyed, it calls this method on the stream, which resets the `OptRef<ExternalProcessorCallbacks>` to prevent use-after-free when deferred stream callbacks arrive after filter destruction.\n\n**`ExternalProcessorClient::start()` signature change:**\n\n```cpp\n// v1.30.0\nExternalProcessorStreamPtr start(\n    ExternalProcessorCallbacks& callbacks,\n    const Grpc::GrpcServiceConfigWithHashKey& config_with_hash_key,\n    const StreamInfo::StreamInfo& stream_info);\n\n// v1.31.0\nExternalProcessorStreamPtr start(\n    ExternalProcessorCallbacks& callbacks,\n    const Grpc::GrpcServiceConfigWithHashKey& config_with_hash_key,\n    const Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions& options,\n    Http::DecoderFilterWatermarkCallbacks* decoder_watermark_callbacks);\n```\n\nThis is an internal API change. It affects anyone who has written a custom `ExternalProcessorClient` implementation (e.g., for testing). The `StreamOptions` now carries parent span, parent context, and buffer-for-retry settings that were previously assembled inside `startStream()`. The `decoder_watermark_callbacks` parameter supports the new flow control feature.\n\n---\n\n## Configuration Updates\n\n### Summary of Proto Field Changes in `ExternalProcessor`\n\n| Field | Number | v1.30 | v1.31 | Action |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| `grpc_service` | 1 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `failure_mode_allow` | 2 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `processing_mode` | 3 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `request_attributes` | 5 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `response_attributes` | 6 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `message_timeout` | 7 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `stat_prefix` | 8 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `mutation_rules` | 9 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `max_message_timeout` | 10 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | 11 | Present | **Deprecated** | Migrate to `route_cache_action` |\n| `forward_rules` | 12 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `filter_metadata` | 13 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `allow_mode_override` | 14 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `disable_immediate_response` | 15 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `metadata_options` | 16 | Present | Present | No change |\n| `observability_mode` | 17 | Present (partial) | Present (full) | Review if using |\n| `route_cache_action` | 18 | **Absent** | **New** | Use instead of `disable_clear_route_cache` |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | 19 | **Absent** | **New** | Configure if using observability mode |\n\n### Minimal v1.30 → v1.31 Configuration Diff\n\nFor a configuration that previously used `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n```yaml\n# Before (v1.30.0)\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      message_timeout: 0.2s\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true    # <-- to migrate\n\n# After (v1.31.0)\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      message_timeout: 0.2s\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN         # <-- replaces disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nFor a configuration using `observability_mode`, add `deferred_close_timeout`:\n\n```yaml\n# Before (v1.30.0)\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n\n# After (v1.31.0) — add deferred_close_timeout\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s   # <-- new; 5s is the default if omitted\n```\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Observability Mode Stream Lifecycle\n\nIn v1.30, the gRPC stream opened in `observability_mode` was closed synchronously when the HTTP filter was destroyed (`onDestroy()`). In v1.31, destruction calls `deferredCloseStream()` instead, which hands the stream to `ThreadLocalStreamManager`. The manager starts a timer and closes the stream after `deferred_close_timeout` elapses. This means:\n\n- External processors in observability mode will continue to receive in-flight data for up to `deferred_close_timeout` after the HTTP request completes.\n- Prometheus/stats: `streams_closed` counter is now incremented by the deferred timer callback, not at filter destruction time.\n\n### 2. Observability Mode Responses Are Silently Discarded\n\nIn v1.31, if an external processor sends a `ProcessingResponse` when `observability_mode = true` was set in the corresponding `ProcessingRequest`, the response is logged and discarded:\n\n```\n// From ext_proc.cc in v1.31:\nif (config_->observabilityMode()) {\n  ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Ignoring received message when observability mode is enabled\");\n  return;\n}\n```\n\nIn v1.30, response handling logic in observability mode was less clearly defined and could lead to unexpected state transitions.\n\n### 3. `openStream()` Now Passes Parent Span and Context\n\nThe `openStream()` call now creates `Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions` with the active span and stream info from the decoder callbacks, enabling proper distributed tracing propagation through the ext_proc gRPC call. In v1.30, only stream info was passed; the parent span was not threaded through.\n\n### 4. Deferred Stream Callback Safety\n\nIn v1.30, if the ext_proc gRPC stream received a message (e.g., `onReceiveMessage`) after the parent filter was destroyed, this could access a dangling reference. In v1.31, `ExternalProcessorStreamImpl::callbacks_` is changed from `ExternalProcessorCallbacks&` (reference) to `OptRef<ExternalProcessorCallbacks>` (optional reference). When `notifyFilterDestroy()` is called, the optional is cleared, and all subsequent callbacks check `callbacks_.has_value()` before dispatching.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Update Proto Definitions and Regenerate Bindings\n\nIf you maintain a custom external processor server or use go-control-plane / Java control plane:\n\n1. Update your dependency on `envoy/api` or `go-control-plane` to a version built from Envoy v1.31 protos.\n2. Regenerate protobuf language bindings.\n3. Fix any compile errors related to `ImmediateResponse.body` type change (`string` → `bytes`).\n\n### Step 2: Update `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`\n\nSearch your Envoy configurations for `disable_clear_route_cache`:\n\n```bash\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/envoy/configs/\n```\n\nFor each occurrence:\n- Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: true` with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- Remove `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (this is equivalent to the default `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`)\n\n**Validation:** Setting both fields simultaneously (e.g., `disable_clear_route_cache: true` and `route_cache_action: CLEAR`) will cause a startup error. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` entirely when using `route_cache_action`.\n\n### Step 3: Update Monitoring for Timeout Errors\n\nUpdate any alerting rules or dashboards that identify ext_proc timeout events by HTTP 500 status code:\n\n1. Change the filter from `response_code == 500` to `response_code == 504` for timeout attribution.\n2. Alternatively, use the `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` access log field matching `ext_proc_error_per-message_timeout_exceeded` — this is stable across the version change.\n\n### Step 4: Configure `deferred_close_timeout` for Observability Mode\n\nIf using `observability_mode: true`, explicitly set `deferred_close_timeout` to match your processor's expected processing latency:\n\n```yaml\n# If your processor needs up to 3 seconds to finalize after stream end:\ndeferred_close_timeout: 3s\n```\n\nIf omitted, the default of 5 seconds applies. In high-traffic environments, tune this value down to limit resource usage from deferred streams.\n\n### Step 5: Update External Processor Servers for Observability Mode\n\nIf your external processor server is used in observability mode, update it to:\n\n1. Check `ProcessingRequest.observability_mode` before sending a `ProcessingResponse`.\n2. Skip sending a response when `observability_mode == true`.\n3. Continue reading from the stream (the stream may stay open longer than the HTTP request lifetime).\n\n### Step 6: Evaluate `grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n\nThe new `grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag is enabled by default. Monitor your ext_proc gRPC stream metrics after upgrading. If you observe unexpected stream pausing or throughput reduction:\n\n1. Check if your external processor is slow to consume data (this is what flow control is protecting against).\n2. If the flag causes issues in your environment, disable it via runtime override while investigating.\n\n### Step 7: Regenerate and Validate Configurations\n\nRun Envoy's configuration validation mode after applying changes:\n\n```bash\nenvoy --mode validate -c /path/to/envoy.yaml\n```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Verify Timeout Error Code\n\nWrite an integration test that:\n1. Configures ext_proc with a very short `message_timeout` (e.g., `1ms`) and `failure_mode_allow: false`.\n2. Points at a mock processor that never responds.\n3. Sends an HTTP request through Envoy.\n4. Asserts the response is **HTTP 504** (not 500).\n\n### 2. Verify `ImmediateResponse.body` Encoding\n\nIf your processor sends `ImmediateResponse` with a body:\n1. Send a request that triggers an immediate response from the processor.\n2. Verify the response body is correctly decoded by the downstream client.\n3. Test with non-ASCII content to confirm binary-safe handling.\n\n### 3. Verify `route_cache_action` Behavior\n\nFor each `route_cache_action` value:\n- **`DEFAULT`:** Verify routing changes only when processor sets `clear_route_cache = true`.\n- **`CLEAR`:** Verify routing is re-evaluated on every ext_proc request header response.\n- **`RETAIN`:** Verify routing is never changed regardless of `clear_route_cache` in processor response.\n\n### 4. Verify Observability Mode Deferred Close\n\nIf using observability mode:\n1. Send a request through Envoy with a processor that logs stream lifecycle events.\n2. Verify the processor continues to receive data after the HTTP stream completes.\n3. Verify the gRPC stream closes within `deferred_close_timeout` after the HTTP stream ends.\n4. Monitor the `streams_closed` stat counter — it should increment after the deferred timeout, not immediately on request completion.\n\n### 5. Verify `disable_clear_route_cache` Backward Compatibility\n\nIf you left `disable_clear_route_cache: true` in your config (without removing it), verify:\n1. Envoy starts without error (it converts it to `RETAIN` internally).\n2. The behavior is equivalent to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\n**Warning:** Do not set both `disable_clear_route_cache: true` and `route_cache_action: CLEAR/RETAIN` simultaneously — this will cause a startup panic.\n\n### 6. Test with Updated go-control-plane / Java Bindings\n\nIf using a control plane:\n1. Build your control plane against the v1.31 proto bindings.\n2. Push an ext_proc configuration and verify Envoy applies it without xDS rejection.\n3. Check xDS logs for any unknown field warnings.\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### Rolling Back to v1.30.0\n\nIf you need to revert from v1.31.0 to v1.30.0 after an upgrade:\n\n**1. Configuration rollback:**\n\n| v1.31 Field | v1.30 Equivalent |\n|---|---|\n| `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | `disable_clear_route_cache: true` |\n| `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | *(omit `disable_clear_route_cache`)* |\n| `route_cache_action: CLEAR` | *(no equivalent — remove and accept DEFAULT behavior)* |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | *(remove field — not recognized by v1.30)* |\n\nRemove `route_cache_action` and `deferred_close_timeout` before deploying v1.30.0. Envoy v1.30 will reject configurations containing unknown fields if strict validation is enabled.\n\n**2. Proto binding rollback:**\n\nRevert `ImmediateResponse.body` back to `string` type in your processor's generated code. Roll back to v1.30 protobuf definitions.\n\n**3. Monitoring rollback:**\n\nRestore any dashboards or alerts that were updated to expect HTTP 504 for ext_proc timeouts back to HTTP 500.\n\n**4. Feature flag rollback:**\n\nThe `grpc_side_stream_flow_control` runtime flag does not exist in v1.30 — remove any runtime override that references it.\n\n### Risk Assessment\n\n| Change | Rollback Risk | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| `route_cache_action` field | Low | Simply remove from config before rolling back |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` field | Low | Remove from config; no behavioral change until observability_mode is also used |\n| `ImmediateResponse.body` type | Medium | Requires proto binding rollback and code recompilation |\n| HTTP 504 timeout response | Low | Purely behavioral; update monitoring before rollback |\n| `grpc_side_stream_flow_control` | Low | Remove runtime override |\n\n---\n\n## Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n1. **Setting both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action`:** This causes a runtime `EnvoyException` at filter construction. Always remove `disable_clear_route_cache` when using `route_cache_action`.\n\n2. **External processor responding in observability mode:** Processors that send `ProcessingResponse` messages when `ProcessingRequest.observability_mode == true` will have their responses silently dropped. This is a behavior change from v1.30 where the response handling was undefined — if your processor relied on sending responses in observability mode, it must be updated.\n\n3. **Assuming `BUFFERED` body mode works in observability mode:** Only `STREAMED` is supported for body processing in observability mode. `BUFFERED` and `BUFFERED_PARTIAL` are silently ignored when `observability_mode = true`. Verify your `processing_mode` configuration.\n\n4. **`deferred_close_timeout` too short for slow processors:** If `deferred_close_timeout` is set lower than the time your processor needs to process the last messages, data may be lost. Monitor `streams_closed` counter timing in relation to request completion to tune this value.\n\n5. **Ignoring the `ImmediateResponse.body` type change in statically-typed languages:** Go and Java will produce compile errors immediately, but dynamically-typed language bindings (e.g., Python with proto3) may silently encode incorrectly. Always regenerate and test bindings explicitly.\n\n6. **Not updating access log parsing for timeout details:** The `%RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS%` string `ext_proc_error_per-message_timeout_exceeded` is unchanged, but the HTTP status code changed from 500 to 504. Any log parsing that uses both fields together for ext_proc timeout detection needs to be updated.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
